<p><b>Brisbane</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/En-au-Brisbane.oga" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" data-file-height="11" data-file-width="11" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-au-Brisbane.oga" title="File:En-au-Brisbane.oga">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'z' in 'Zion'">z</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ən/ 'on' in 'button'">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_capital_cities" title="List of Australian capital cities">capital</a> and most populous city in the <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">Australian state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qpn_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-qpn-9">[9]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Australia_by_population" title="List of cities in Australia by population">third most populous city</a> in Australia. Brisbane's metropolitan area has a population of 2.3 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABSGCCSA_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABSGCCSA-1">[1]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Queensland" title="South East Queensland">South East Queensland</a> <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">urban conurbation</a>, centred on Brisbane, encompasses a population of more than 3.4 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABSERP13_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABSERP13-10">[10]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_central_business_district" title="Brisbane central business district">Brisbane central business district</a> stands on the <a href="/wiki/Early_Streets_of_Brisbane" title="Early Streets of Brisbane">original European settlement</a> and is situated inside a <a href="/wiki/Meander" title="Meander">bend</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River" title="Brisbane River">Brisbane River</a>, about 15 kilometres (9 miles) from its mouth at <a href="/wiki/Moreton_Bay" title="Moreton Bay">Moreton Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The metropolitan area extends in all directions along the <a href="/wiki/Floodplain" title="Floodplain">floodplain</a> of the Brisbane River Valley between Moreton Bay and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dividing_Range" title="Great Dividing Range">Great Dividing Range</a>, sprawling across several of Australia's most populous <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Australia" title="Local government in Australia">local government areas</a> (LGAs), most centrally the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brisbane" title="City of Brisbane">City of Brisbane</a>, which is by far the most populous LGA in the nation. The <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> of Brisbane is Brisbanite.</p>
<p>One of the oldest cities in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, Brisbane was founded upon the ancient homelands of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Turrbal" title="Turrbal">Turrbal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jagera" title="Jagera">Jagera</a> peoples. Named after the Brisbane River on which it is located – which in turn was named after Scotsman <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brisbane" title="Thomas Brisbane">Sir Thomas Brisbane</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_South_Wales" title="Governor of New South Wales">Governor of New South Wales</a> from 1821 to 1825<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qpn_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-qpn-9">[9]</a></sup> – the area was chosen as a place for secondary offenders from the <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney Colony</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal settlement</a> was founded in 1824 at <a href="/wiki/Redcliffe,_Queensland" title="Redcliffe, Queensland">Redcliffe</a>, 28 kilometres (17 mi) north of the central business district, but was soon abandoned and moved to <a href="/wiki/North_Quay,_Brisbane" title="North Quay, Brisbane">North Quay</a> in 1825, opening to free settlement in 1842. The city was marred by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_frontier_wars" title="Australian frontier wars">Australian frontier wars</a> between 1843 and 1855, and development was partly set back by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_Brisbane" title="Great Fire of Brisbane">Great Fire of Brisbane</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/1893_Brisbane_flood" title="1893 Brisbane flood">Great Brisbane Flood</a>. Brisbane was chosen as the capital <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_Queensland" title="Separation of Queensland">when Queensland was proclaimed a separate colony</a> from <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> in 1859. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Brisbane played a central role in the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> campaign and served as the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Pacific_Area_(command)" title="South West Pacific Area (command)">South West Pacific</a> headquarters for United States Army <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">General Douglas MacArthur</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Today, Brisbane is well known for its distinct <a href="/wiki/Queenslander_(architecture)" title="Queenslander (architecture)">Queenslander architecture</a> which forms much of the city's built heritage. It also receives attention for its damaging <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flood</a> events, most notably in <a href="/wiki/1974_Brisbane_flood" title="1974 Brisbane flood">1974</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Queensland_floods" title="2010–11 Queensland floods">2011</a>. The city is <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brisbane" title="Tourism in Brisbane">a popular tourist destination</a>, serving as a gateway to the state of Queensland, particularly to the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Coast,_Queensland" title="Sunshine Coast, Queensland">Sunshine Coast</a>, popular <a href="/wiki/Resort_town" title="Resort town">resort areas</a> immediately south and north of Brisbane, respectively. Several large cultural, international and sporting events have been held at Brisbane, including the <a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982 Commonwealth Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Expo_88" title="World Expo 88">World Expo '88</a>, the final <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Games" title="Goodwill Games">Goodwill Games</a> <a href="/wiki/2001_Goodwill_Games" title="2001 Goodwill Games">in 2001</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2014_G20_Brisbane_summit" title="2014 G20 Brisbane summit">2014 G-20 summit</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brisbane" title="History of Brisbane">History of Brisbane</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nineteenth_century">Nineteenth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Nineteenth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The-Windmill-1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1048" data-file-width="927" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The-Windmill-1.JPG/170px-The-Windmill-1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The-Windmill-1.JPG/255px-The-Windmill-1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/The-Windmill-1.JPG/340px-The-Windmill-1.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The-Windmill-1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/The_Old_Windmill,_Brisbane" title="The Old Windmill, Brisbane">The Old Windmill</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wickham_Park,_Brisbane" title="Wickham Park, Brisbane">Wickham Park</a>, built by convicts in 1828</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia_(1788%E2%80%931850)" title="History of Australia (1788–1850)">white settlement</a>, the Brisbane area was inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Turrbal" title="Turrbal">Turrbal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jagera" title="Jagera">Jagera</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> They knew the area that is now the central business district as Mian-jin, meaning "place shaped as a spike".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Moreton_Bay" title="Moreton Bay">Moreton Bay</a> area was initially explored by <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Flinders" title="Matthew Flinders">Matthew Flinders</a>. On 17 July 1799, Flinders landed at what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Woody_Point,_Queensland" title="Woody Point, Queensland">Woody Point</a>, which he named "Red Cliff Point" after the red-coloured cliffs visible from the bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1823 <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_South_Wales" title="Governor of New South Wales">Governor of New South Wales</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brisbane" title="Thomas Brisbane">Thomas Brisbane</a> instructed that a new northern <a href="/wiki/Convicts_in_Australia" title="Convicts in Australia">penal settlement</a> be developed, and an exploration party led by <a href="/wiki/John_Oxley" title="John Oxley">John Oxley</a> further explored Moreton Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seqhistory.com_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-seqhistory.com-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Oxley discovered, named, and explored the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River" title="Brisbane River">Brisbane River</a> as far as <a href="/wiki/Goodna,_Queensland" title="Goodna, Queensland">Goodna</a>, 20 kilometres (12 mi) upstream from the Brisbane central business district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seqhistory.com_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-seqhistory.com-16">[16]</a></sup> Oxley recommended Red Cliff Point for the new colony, reporting that ships could land at any tide and easily get close to the shore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The party settled in <a href="/wiki/Redcliffe,_Queensland" title="Redcliffe, Queensland">Redcliffe</a> on 13 September 1824, under the command of Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Henry_Miller_(commandant)" title="Henry Miller (commandant)">Henry Miller</a> with 14 soldiers (some with wives and children) and 29 convicts. However, this settlement was abandoned after a year and the colony was moved to a site on the Brisbane River now known as <a href="/wiki/North_Quay,_Brisbane" title="North Quay, Brisbane">North Quay</a>, 28 km (17 mi) south, which offered a more reliable water supply. Sir Thomas Brisbane visited the settlement and travelled 28 miles up the Brisbane River in December 1824, bestowing upon Brisbane the distinction of being the only Australian capital city set foot upon by its namesake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Chief Justice Forbes gave the new settlement the name of Edenglassie before it was named Brisbane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seeing_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-seeing-19">[19]</a></sup> Non-convict European settlement of the Brisbane region commenced in 1838.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> German missionaries settled at Zions Hill, <a href="/wiki/Nundah,_Queensland" title="Nundah, Queensland">Nundah</a> as early as 1837, five years before Brisbane was officially declared a free settlement. The band consisted of ministers <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Eipper" title="Christopher Eipper">Christopher Eipper</a> (1813–1894) and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Wilhelm_Schmidt" title="Carl Wilhelm Schmidt">Carl Wilhelm Schmidt</a> and lay missionaries Haussmann, Johann Gottried Wagner, Niquet, Hartenstein, Zillman, Franz, Rode, Doege and Schneider.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> They were allocated 260 hectares and set about establishing the mission, which became known as the German Station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Later in the 1860s many German immigrants from the <a href="/wiki/Uckermark" title="Uckermark">Uckermark</a> region in <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> as well as other German regions settled in the <a href="/wiki/Bethania,_Queensland" title="Bethania, Queensland">Bethania-</a> <a href="/wiki/Beenleigh,_Queensland" title="Beenleigh, Queensland">Beenleigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darling_Downs" title="Darling Downs">Darling Downs</a> areas. These immigrants were selected and assisted through immigration programs established by <a href="/wiki/John_Dunmore_Lang" title="John Dunmore Lang">John Dunmore Lang</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Heussler" title="John Heussler">Johann Christian Heussler</a> and were offered free passage, good wages and selections of land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The penal settlement under the control of Captain <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Logan" title="Patrick Logan">Patrick Logan</a> flourished with the numbers of convicts increasing dramatically from around 200 to over 1000 men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25">[25]</a></sup> He created a substantial settlement of brick and stone buildings, complete with school and hospital. He formed additional outstations and made several important journeys of exploration. He is also infamous for his extreme use of the <a href="/wiki/Cat_o%27_nine_tails" title="Cat o' nine tails">Cat o' nine tails</a> on convicts. The maximum allowed limit of lashes was 50 however Logan regularly applied sentences of 150 lashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Free settlers entered the area over the following five years and by the end of 1840 <a href="/wiki/Robert_Dixon_(explorer)" title="Robert Dixon (explorer)">Robert Dixon</a> began work on the first plan of Brisbane Town, in anticipation of future development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Queensland was <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_Queensland" title="Separation of Queensland">separated from New South Wales</a> by Letters Patent dated 6 June 1859, proclaimed by Sir George Ferguson Bowen on 10 December 1859, whereupon he became Queensland's first governor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> with Brisbane chosen as its capital, although it was not incorporated as a city until 1902.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twentieth_century">Twentieth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Twentieth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street,_Brisbane,_during_World_War_II.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="713" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street%2C_Brisbane%2C_during_World_War_II.jpg/170px-StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street%2C_Brisbane%2C_during_World_War_II.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street%2C_Brisbane%2C_during_World_War_II.jpg/255px-StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street%2C_Brisbane%2C_during_World_War_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street%2C_Brisbane%2C_during_World_War_II.jpg/340px-StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street%2C_Brisbane%2C_during_World_War_II.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:StateLibQld_1_126407_R.A.A.F._recruits_marching_along_Queen_Street,_Brisbane,_during_World_War_II.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Air_Force" title="Royal Australian Air Force">Royal Australian Air Force</a> recruits marching along Queen Street, August 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over twenty small municipalities and shires were amalgamated in 1925 to form the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brisbane" title="City of Brisbane">City of Brisbane</a>, governed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane_City_Council" title="Brisbane City Council">Brisbane City Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> 1930 was a significant year for Brisbane with the completion of <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_City_Hall" title="Brisbane City Hall">Brisbane City Hall</a>, then the city's tallest building and the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_Remembrance,_Brisbane" title="Shrine of Remembrance, Brisbane">Shrine of Remembrance</a>, in <a href="/wiki/ANZAC_Square,_Brisbane" title="ANZAC Square, Brisbane">ANZAC Square</a>, which has become Brisbane's main <a href="/wiki/War_memorial" title="War memorial">war memorial</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> These historic buildings, along with the <a href="/wiki/Story_Bridge" title="Story Bridge">Story Bridge</a> which opened in 1940, are key landmarks that help define the architectural character of the city.</p>
<p>During World War II, Brisbane became central to the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> campaign when the AMP Building (now called <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Central" title="MacArthur Central">MacArthur Central</a>) was used as the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Pacific_Area_(command)#Command" title="South West Pacific Area (command)">South West Pacific headquarters</a> for <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">General Douglas MacArthur</a>, chief of the Allied Pacific forces, until his headquarters were moved to <a href="/wiki/Jayapura" title="Jayapura">Hollandia</a> in August 1944. MacArthur had previously rejected use of the University of Queensland complex as his headquarters, as the distinctive bends in the river at St Lucia could have aided enemy bombers. Also used as a headquarters by the American troops during World War II was the <a href="/wiki/T_%26_G_Building,_Brisbane" title="T &amp; G Building, Brisbane">T &amp; G Building</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> About one million US troops passed through Australia during the war, as the primary co-ordination point for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_West_Pacific_Area" title="South West Pacific Area">South West Pacific</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In 1942 Brisbane was the site of a violent clash between visiting US military personnel and Australian servicemen and civilians which resulted in one death and hundreds of injuries. This incident became known colloquially as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Brisbane" title="Battle of Brisbane">Battle of Brisbane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Postwar Brisbane had developed a "big country town" stigma, an image the city's politicians and marketers were very keen to remove.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In the late 1950s an anonymous poet known as The Brisbane Bard generated much attention on the city which helped shake this stigma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Despite steady growth, Brisbane's development was punctuated by infrastructure problems. The State government under <a href="/wiki/Joh_Bjelke-Petersen" title="Joh Bjelke-Petersen">Joh Bjelke-Petersen</a> began a major program of change and <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a>, beginning with the central business district and inner suburbs. <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Brisbane" title="Trams in Brisbane">Trams in Brisbane</a> were a popular mode of public transport until the network was closed in 1969, leaving Melbourne as the last Australian city to operate a tram network until recently.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1974_Brisbane_flood" title="1974 Brisbane flood">1974 Brisbane flood</a> was a major disaster which temporarily crippled the city. During this era, Brisbane grew and modernised rapidly becoming a destination of interstate migration. Some of Brisbane's popular landmarks were lost, including the <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_Hotel,_Brisbane" title="Bellevue Hotel, Brisbane">Bellevue Hotel</a> in 1979 and <a href="/wiki/Cloudland" title="Cloudland">Cloudland</a> in 1982, demolished in controversial circumstances by the Deen Brothers demolition crew. Major public works included the <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Expressway" title="Riverside Expressway">Riverside Expressway</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gateway_Bridge" title="Gateway Bridge">Gateway Bridge</a>, and later, the redevelopment of <a href="/wiki/South_Bank,_Queensland" title="South Bank, Queensland">South Bank</a>, starting with the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Art_Gallery" title="Queensland Art Gallery">Queensland Art Gallery</a>.</p>
<p>Brisbane hosted the <a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982 Commonwealth Games</a> and the 1988 World Exposition (known locally as <a href="/wiki/World_Expo_88" title="World Expo 88">World Expo 88</a>). These events were accompanied by a scale of public expenditure, construction and development not previously seen in the state of Queensland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Brisbane's population growth has exceeded the national average every year since 1990 at an average rate of around 2.2% per year.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:608px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Expo_88_(8075991938).jpg" title="A panorama view of the stage and Brisbane River during World Expo 88"><img alt="" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="900" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Expo_88_%288075991938%29.jpg/600px-Expo_88_%288075991938%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Expo_88_%288075991938%29.jpg 1.5x" width="600"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Expo_88_(8075991938).jpg" title="File:Expo 88 (8075991938).jpg"></a></div>
A panorama view of the stage and Brisbane River during <a href="/wiki/World_Expo_88" title="World Expo 88">World Expo 88</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty-first_century">Twenty-first century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Twenty-first century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After two decades of record population growth, Brisbane was hit again by a major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Queensland_floods" title="2010–2011 Queensland floods">flood in January 2011</a>. The Brisbane River did not reach the same height as the previous 1974 flood but still caused extensive damage and disruption to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Berry_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Berry-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brisbane also gained further international recognition, hosting the final <a href="/wiki/2001_Goodwill_Games" title="2001 Goodwill Games">Goodwill Games</a> in 2001, and also some of the games in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2014_G20_Brisbane_summit" title="2014 G20 Brisbane summit">2014 G20 Brisbane summit</a>.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Night_skyline_of_Brisbane,_Queensland,_Australia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="797" data-file-width="2000" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Night_skyline_of_Brisbane%2C_Queensland%2C_Australia.jpg/600px-Night_skyline_of_Brisbane%2C_Queensland%2C_Australia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Night_skyline_of_Brisbane%2C_Queensland%2C_Australia.jpg/900px-Night_skyline_of_Brisbane%2C_Queensland%2C_Australia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Night_skyline_of_Brisbane%2C_Queensland%2C_Australia.jpg/1200px-Night_skyline_of_Brisbane%2C_Queensland%2C_Australia.jpg 2x" width="600"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Night_skyline_of_Brisbane,_Queensland,_Australia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The night skyline of Brisbane's central business district from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Coot-tha" title="Mount Coot-tha">Mount Coot-tha</a>, May 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="799" data-file-width="790" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg/220px-Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg/330px-Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg/440px-Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Aerial_From_Satellite.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite image of Brisbane Metropolitan Area</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane is in the southeast corner of Queensland. The city is centred along the Brisbane River, and its eastern suburbs line the shores of Moreton Bay. The greater Brisbane region is on the coastal plain east of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dividing_Range" title="Great Dividing Range">Great Dividing Range</a>. Brisbane's metropolitan area sprawls along the Moreton Bay floodplain from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caboolture" title="Caboolture">Caboolture</a> in the north to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beenleigh" title="Beenleigh">Beenleigh</a> in the south, and across to <a href="/wiki/Ipswich,_Queensland" title="Ipswich, Queensland">Ipswich</a> in the south west.</p>
<p>The city of Brisbane is hilly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thenandnow_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-thenandnow-41">[41]</a></sup> The urban area, including the central business district, are partially elevated by spurs of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taylor_Range_(Queensland)" title="Taylor Range (Queensland)">Herbert Taylor Range</a>, such as the summit of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Coot-tha,_Queensland" title="Mount Coot-tha, Queensland">Mount Coot-tha</a>, reaching up to 300 metres (980 ft) and the smaller <a href="/wiki/Enoggera_Hill" title="Enoggera Hill">Enoggera Hill</a>. Other prominent rises in Brisbane are <a href="/wiki/Mount_Gravatt,_Queensland" title="Mount Gravatt, Queensland">Mount Gravatt</a> and nearby <a href="/wiki/Toohey_Mountain" title="Toohey Mountain">Toohey Mountain</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Petrie" title="Mount Petrie">Mount Petrie</a> at 170 m (560 ft) and the lower rises of <a href="/wiki/Highgate_Hill,_Queensland" title="Highgate Hill, Queensland">Highgate Hill</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Ommaney" title="Mount Ommaney">Mount Ommaney</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephens_Mountain,_Queensland" title="Stephens Mountain, Queensland">Stephens Mountain</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whites_Hill,_Queensland" title="Whites Hill, Queensland">Whites Hill</a> are dotted across the city. Also, on the west, are the higher Mount Glorious, (680 m), and Mount Nebo (550 m).</p>
<p>The city is on a low-lying <a href="/wiki/Floodplain" title="Floodplain">floodplain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Many suburban creeks criss-cross the city, increasing the risk of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flooding" title="Flooding">flooding</a>. The city has suffered three major floods since colonisation, in <a href="/wiki/1893_Brisbane_flood" title="1893 Brisbane flood">February 1893</a>, January 1974, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Queensland_floods" title="2010–2011 Queensland floods">January 2011</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1974_Brisbane_Flood" title="1974 Brisbane Flood">1974 Brisbane Flood</a> occurred partly as a result of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclone_Wanda" title="Cyclone Wanda">Cyclone Wanda</a>". Heavy rain had fallen continuously for three weeks before the <a href="/wiki/Australia_Day" title="Australia Day">Australia Day</a> weekend flood (26–27 January 1974).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The flood damaged many parts of the city, especially the suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Oxley,_Queensland" title="Oxley, Queensland">Oxley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulimba,_Queensland" title="Bulimba, Queensland">Bulimba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocklea,_Queensland" title="Rocklea, Queensland">Rocklea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coorparoo,_Queensland" title="Coorparoo, Queensland">Coorparoo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toowong,_Queensland" title="Toowong, Queensland">Toowong</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Farm,_Queensland" title="New Farm, Queensland">New Farm</a>. The <a href="/wiki/City_Botanic_Gardens" title="City Botanic Gardens">City Botanic Gardens</a> were inundated, leading to a new colony of <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a> forming in the City Reach of the Brisbane River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_structure">Urban structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Urban structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:172px;max-width:172px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg/170px-BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg/255px-BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg/340px-BNE-StoryBridge-fromCityCat.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:232px;max-width:232px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Story_Bridge,_Brisbane_(14964432888).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3234" data-file-width="5749" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Story_Bridge%2C_Brisbane_%2814964432888%29.jpg/230px-Story_Bridge%2C_Brisbane_%2814964432888%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Story_Bridge%2C_Brisbane_%2814964432888%29.jpg/345px-Story_Bridge%2C_Brisbane_%2814964432888%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Story_Bridge%2C_Brisbane_%2814964432888%29.jpg/460px-Story_Bridge%2C_Brisbane_%2814964432888%29.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left/right/center;background-color:">The steel <a href="/wiki/Cantilever_bridge" title="Cantilever bridge">cantilever</a> <a href="/wiki/Story_Bridge" title="Story Bridge">Story Bridge</a> was constructed in 1940 to connect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fortitude_Valley" title="Fortitude Valley">Fortitude Valley</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_Point,_Queensland" title="Kangaroo Point, Queensland">Kangaroo Point</a>. In the image on the right, the bridge is illuminated in blue for <a href="/wiki/Ovarian_cancer" title="Ovarian cancer">ovarian cancer</a> awareness.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Brisbane central business district (CBD) lies in a curve of the Brisbane river. The CBD covers 2.2 km<sup>2</sup> (0.8 sq mi) and is walkable. Central streets are named after members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">royal family</a>. <a href="/wiki/Queen_Street,_Brisbane" title="Queen Street, Brisbane">Queen Street</a> is Brisbane's traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Main_street" title="Main street">main street</a>. Streets named after female members (<a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Street,_Brisbane" title="Adelaide Street, Brisbane">Adelaide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alice_Street,_Brisbane" title="Alice Street, Brisbane">Alice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ann_Street,_Brisbane" title="Ann Street, Brisbane">Ann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Street,_Brisbane" title="Charlotte Street, Brisbane">Charlotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Street,_Brisbane" title="Elizabeth Street, Brisbane">Elizabeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Street,_Brisbane" title="Margaret Street, Brisbane">Margaret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Street,_Brisbane" title="Mary Street, Brisbane">Mary</a>) run parallel to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Street,_Brisbane" title="Queen Street, Brisbane">Queen Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Street_Mall,_Brisbane" title="Queen Street Mall, Brisbane">Queen Street Mall</a> (named in honour of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>) and at right angles to streets named after male members (<a href="/wiki/Albert_Street,_Brisbane" title="Albert Street, Brisbane">Albert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Street,_Brisbane" title="Edward Street, Brisbane">Edward</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Street,_Brisbane" title="George Street, Brisbane">George</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Street,_Brisbane" title="William Street, Brisbane">William</a>). The city has retained some heritage buildings dating back to the 1820s. <a href="/wiki/The_Old_Windmill,_Brisbane" title="The Old Windmill, Brisbane">The Old Windmill</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Wickham_Park,_Brisbane" title="Wickham Park, Brisbane">Wickham Park</a>, built by convict labour in 1824,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldwindmill_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-oldwindmill-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> is the oldest surviving building in Brisbane. The Old Windmill was originally used for the grinding of grain and a punishment for the convicts who manually operated the grinding mill. The Old Windmill tower's other significant claim to fame, largely ignored, is that the first television signals in the southern hemisphere were transmitted from it by experimenters in April 1934—long before TV commenced in most places. These experimental TV broadcasts continued until World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldwindmill_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-oldwindmill-45">[45]</a></sup> The Old Commissariat Store, on William Street, built by convict labour in 1828, was originally used partly as a grainhouse, has also been a hostel for immigrants and used for the storage of records. Built with <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_tuff" title="Brisbane tuff">Brisbane tuff</a> from the nearby <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_Point_Cliffs" title="Kangaroo Point Cliffs">Kangaroo Point Cliffs</a> and sandstone from a quarry near today's Albion Park Racecourse, it is now the home of the Royal Historical Society of Brisbane. It contains a museum and can also be hired for small functions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Greater Brisbane had a density of 140 people per square kilometre in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Like many western cities, Brisbane sprawls into the greater metropolitan area. This results from the fact that most of Brisbane's housing stock consists of detached houses.</p>
<p>Early legislation decreed a minimum size for residential blocks causing few <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrace_house" title="Terrace house">terrace houses</a> being constructed in Brisbane. Recently the density of the city and <a href="/wiki/Inner_city" title="Inner city">inner city</a> neighbourhoods has increased with the construction of apartments, with the result that the population of the central business district has doubled over the last 5 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popg_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-popg-51">[51]</a></sup> The high density housing that historically existed came in the form of miniature <a href="/wiki/Queenslander_(architecture)" title="Queenslander (architecture)">Queenslander</a>-style houses which resemble the much larger traditional styles but are sometimes only one quarter the size. These miniature Queenslanders are becoming scarce but can still be seen in the inner city suburbs. Multi residence accommodations (such as apartment blocks) are relatively new to Brisbane, with few such blocks built before 1970, other than in inner suburbs such as <a href="/wiki/New_Farm,_Queensland" title="New Farm, Queensland">New Farm</a>. Pre-1950 housing was often built in a distinctive architectural style known as a <a href="/wiki/Queenslander_(architecture)" title="Queenslander (architecture)">Queenslander</a>, featuring timber construction with large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verandah" title="Verandah">verandahs</a> and high ceilings. The relatively low cost of timber in South-East Queensland meant that until recently most residences were constructed of timber, rather than brick or stone. Many of these houses are elevated on stumps (also called "stilts"), that were originally timber, but are now frequently replaced by steel or concrete. Brisbane is home to several of <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Australia" title="List of tallest buildings in Australia">Australia's tallest buildings</a>. <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Brisbane" title="List of tallest buildings in Brisbane">Brisbane's tallest building</a> is <a href="/wiki/1_William_Street,_Brisbane" title="1 William Street, Brisbane">1 William Street</a> at 260 metres, to be overtaken by the 270 metre <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Skytower" title="Brisbane Skytower">Brisbane Skytower</a> which is currently under construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_storm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="647" data-file-width="973" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Brisbane_storm.jpg/220px-Brisbane_storm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Brisbane_storm.jpg/330px-Brisbane_storm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Brisbane_storm.jpg/440px-Brisbane_storm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_storm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A spring storm with lightning over the central business district</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <i>Cfa</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> with hot, humid summers and dry moderately warm winters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Due to its proximity to the Coral Sea and a warm ocean current, Brisbane's overall temperature variability is somewhat less than most other Australian capitals, particularly in winter, when maximum temperatures below 20 °C (68 °F) are relatively uncommon (compared with Sydney, Melbourne, Adelaide, and Perth). From November to March, thunderstorms are common over Brisbane, with the more severe events accompanied by large damaging hail stones, torrential rain and destructive winds. On an annual basis, Brisbane averages 124 clear days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Dewpoints in the summer average at around 20 °C (68.0 °F); the <a href="/wiki/Apparent_temperature" title="Apparent temperature">apparent temperature</a> exceeds 30 °C (86.0 °F) on almost all summer days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's highest recorded temperature was 43.2 °C (110 °F) on 26 January 1940,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-58">[58]</a></sup> but temperatures above 38 °C (100 °F) are uncommon. On 19 July 2007, Brisbane's temperature fell below the freezing point for the first time since records began, registering −0.1 °C (32 °F) at the airport station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The city station has never dropped below 2 °C (35.6 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-57">[57]</a></sup> with the average coldest night during winter being around 6 °C (42.8 °F), however locations directly west of Brisbane such as <a href="/wiki/Ipswich,_Queensland" title="Ipswich, Queensland">Ipswich</a> have dropped as low as −5 °C (23 °F) with heavy ground frost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In 2009 Brisbane recorded its hottest winter day at 35.4 °C (96 °F) on 24 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The average July day however is around 22 °C (72 °F) with sunny skies and low humidity, occasionally as high as 27 °C (81 °F), whilst maximum temperatures below 18 °C (64 °F) are usually associated with brief but not uncommon periods of cloud and winter rain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brisbane's wettest day occurred on 21 January 1887, when 465 millimetres (18.3 in) of rain fell on the city, the highest maximum daily rainfall of Australia's capital cities. The highest minimum temperature ever recorded in Brisbane was 28.0 °C (82.4 °F) on 29 January 1940 and again on 21 January 2017, whilst the lowest maximum temperature was 10.2 °C (50.4 °F) on the 12 August 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 2001 until 2010, Brisbane and surrounding temperate areas had been experiencing the most severe drought in over a century, with dam levels dropping to 16.9% of their capacity on 10 August 2007. Residents were mandated by local laws to observe <a href="/wiki/Water_restrictions_in_Australia#Stages" title="Water restrictions in Australia">level 6</a> water restrictions on gardening and other outdoor water usage. Per capita water usage is below 140 litres per day, giving Brisbane one of the lowest per capita usages of water of any developed city in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> On 9 January 2011, an upper low crossed north of Brisbane and dropped rainfall on an already saturated southeast coast of Queensland, resulting in severe flooding and damage in Brisbane and the surrounding area;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> the same storm season also caused the water storage to climb to over 98% of maximum capacity and broke the drought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Water restrictions have been replaced with water conservation measures that aim at a target of 200 litres per day/per person, but consumption is rarely over 160 litres. In November 2011, Brisbane saw 22 days with no recorded rainfall, which was the driest start to a November since 1919.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CourierMail_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-CourierMail-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brisbane also lies in the Tropical Cyclone risk area, although cyclones are rare. The last to affect Brisbane but not directly cross the city was Tropical Cyclone Hamish in March 2009: it remained 350 km (220 mi) north of Brisbane<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-66">[66]</a></sup> but caused significant damage to beaches as well as an oil spill outside <a href="/wiki/Moreton_Bay" title="Moreton Bay">Moreton Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ES1_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-ES1-67">[67]</a></sup> Average annual temperature of the sea is 24 °C (75 °F), from 21 °C (70 °F) in July to 27 °C (81 °F) in February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weather2travel_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-68">[68]</a></sup> The city is susceptible to severe thunderstorms in the spring and summer months; on 16 November 2008 a severe storm caused tremendous damage in the outer suburbs, most notably <a href="/wiki/The_Gap,_Queensland" title="The Gap, Queensland">The Gap</a>. Roofs were torn off houses and hundreds of trees were felled. More recently, on 27 November 2014, a very strong <a href="/wiki/2014_Brisbane_hailstorm" title="2014 Brisbane hailstorm">storm</a> made a direct hit on the city centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCNEWS_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNEWS-69">[69]</a></sup> Described as 'the worst storm in a decade,' very large hail smashed skyscraper windows while a flash flood tore through the CBD. Wind gusts of 141 km/h (88 mph) were recorded in some suburbs, many houses were severely damaged, cars were destroyed and planes were flipped at the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Airport" title="Brisbane Airport">Brisbane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archerfield_Airport" title="Archerfield Airport">Archerfield Airports</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCNEWS_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNEWS-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dust_storm" title="Dust storm">Dust storms</a> in Brisbane are extremely rare; on 23 September 2009, however, a <a href="/wiki/2009_Australian_dust_storm" title="2009 Australian dust storm">severe dust storm</a> blanketed Brisbane, as well as other parts of eastern Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brisbane" title="City of Brisbane">City of Brisbane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Queensland" title="Government of Queensland">Government of Queensland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:393px;max-width:393px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3038" data-file-width="2025" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg/150px-Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg/225px-Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg/300px-Brisbane_Town_Hall.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:237px;max-width:237px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House,_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="2559" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Parliament_House%2C_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg/235px-Parliament_House%2C_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Parliament_House%2C_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg/353px-Parliament_House%2C_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Parliament_House%2C_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg/470px-Parliament_House%2C_Brisbane_03-cropped.jpg 2x" width="235"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left/right/center;background-color:"><a href="/wiki/Brisbane_City_Hall" title="Brisbane City Hall">Brisbane City Hall</a> home to the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Brisbane" title="Museum of Brisbane">Museum of Brisbane</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane_City_Council" title="Brisbane City Council">Brisbane City Council</a> offices and <a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Brisbane" title="Parliament House, Brisbane">Parliament House</a>, the home of Queensland's state legislature</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Unlike other Australian capital cities, a large portion of the greater metropolitan area, or Greater Capital City Statistical Area (GCCSA, formerly statistical division), of Brisbane is controlled by a single <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Australia" title="Local government in Australia">local government area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brisbane" title="City of Brisbane">City of Brisbane</a>. Since the creation of the City of Brisbane in 1925 the urban areas of Brisbane have expanded considerably past the council boundaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The City is by far the largest local government body (in terms of population and budget) in Australia, serving almost half the GCCSA's population. It was formed by the merger of twenty smaller LGAs in 1925, and covers an area of 1,367 km<sup>2</sup> (528 sq mi).</p>
<p>The Council's annual budget is about AUD 1.6 billion, and it has an asset base of AUD 13 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The remainder of the metropolitan area falls into the LGAs of <a href="/wiki/Logan_City" title="Logan City">Logan City</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Moreton_Bay_Region" title="Moreton Bay Region">Moreton Bay Region</a> in the northern suburbs, the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Ipswich" title="City of Ipswich">City of Ipswich</a> to the south west, <a href="/wiki/Redland_City" title="Redland City">Redland City</a> to the south east on the bayside, with a small strip to the far west in the <a href="/wiki/Scenic_Rim_Region" title="Scenic Rim Region">Scenic Rim Region</a>. The current Lord Mayor of Brisbane is <a href="/wiki/Graham_Quirk" title="Graham Quirk">Graham Quirk</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_National_Party_of_Queensland" title="Liberal National Party of Queensland">Liberal National Party of Queensland</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_city_skyline,_May_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1226" data-file-width="4365" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brisbane_city_skyline%2C_May_2013.jpg/280px-Brisbane_city_skyline%2C_May_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brisbane_city_skyline%2C_May_2013.jpg/420px-Brisbane_city_skyline%2C_May_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Brisbane_city_skyline%2C_May_2013.jpg/560px-Brisbane_city_skyline%2C_May_2013.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_city_skyline,_May_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brisbane skyline; <a href="/wiki/Infinity_Tower_(Brisbane)" title="Infinity Tower (Brisbane)">Infinity Tower</a> under construction on the far right</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>White-collar industries include information technology, <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, higher education and <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> administration generally concentrated in and around the central business district and recently established office areas in the inner suburbs. Blue-collar industries, including petroleum refining, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stevedoring" title="Stevedoring">stevedoring</a>, paper milling, <a href="/wiki/Metalworking" title="Metalworking">metalworking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Rail" title="Queensland Rail">QR</a> railway workshops, tend to be located on the lower reaches of the Brisbane River and in new industrial zones on the urban fringe. Tourism is an important part of the Brisbane economy, both in its own right and as a gateway to other areas of Queensland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ABS-6291.0.55.001-LabourForceAustraliaDetailed_ElectronicDelivery-LabourForceStatusByLabourMarketRegionSex-GreaterBrisbane-UnemploymentRate-Persons-A84600151F.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="512" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/ABS-6291.0.55.001-LabourForceAustraliaDetailed_ElectronicDelivery-LabourForceStatusByLabourMarketRegionSex-GreaterBrisbane-UnemploymentRate-Persons-A84600151F.svg/300px-thumbnail.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/ABS-6291.0.55.001-LabourForceAustraliaDetailed_ElectronicDelivery-LabourForceStatusByLabourMarketRegionSex-GreaterBrisbane-UnemploymentRate-Persons-A84600151F.svg/450px-thumbnail.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/ABS-6291.0.55.001-LabourForceAustraliaDetailed_ElectronicDelivery-LabourForceStatusByLabourMarketRegionSex-GreaterBrisbane-UnemploymentRate-Persons-A84600151F.svg/600px-thumbnail.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ABS-6291.0.55.001-LabourForceAustraliaDetailed_ElectronicDelivery-LabourForceStatusByLabourMarketRegionSex-GreaterBrisbane-UnemploymentRate-Persons-A84600151F.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Unemployment rate in the Greater Brisbane labour market region since 1998<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the late 1990s and early 2000s, the Queensland State Government has been developing technology and science industries in Queensland as a whole, and Brisbane in particular, as part of its "Smart State" initiative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The government has invested in several biotechnology and research facilities at several universities in Brisbane. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_for_Molecular_Bioscience" title="Institute for Molecular Bioscience">Institute for Molecular Bioscience</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Queensland" title="University of Queensland">University of Queensland</a> (UQ) Saint Lucia Campus is a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSIRO" title="CSIRO">CSIRO</a> and Queensland state government initiative for research and innovation that is currently being emulated at the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_University_of_Technology" title="Queensland University of Technology">Queensland University of Technology</a> (QUT) Campus at Kelvin Grove with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Health_and_Biomedical_Innovation" title="Institute of Health and Biomedical Innovation">Institute of Health and Biomedical Innovation</a> (IHBI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Australia_Bank,_Brisbane.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/National_Australia_Bank%2C_Brisbane.jpg/220px-National_Australia_Bank%2C_Brisbane.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/National_Australia_Bank%2C_Brisbane.jpg/330px-National_Australia_Bank%2C_Brisbane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/National_Australia_Bank%2C_Brisbane.jpg/440px-National_Australia_Bank%2C_Brisbane.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Australia_Bank,_Brisbane.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/National_Australia_Bank_Building" title="National Australia Bank Building">National Australia Bank Building</a> located on <a href="/wiki/Queen_Street,_Brisbane" title="Queen Street, Brisbane">Queen Street</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane is one of the major business hubs in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Most major Australian companies, as well as numerous international companies, have contact offices in Brisbane, while numerous <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a> businesses have distribution hubs in and around the city. <a href="/wiki/DHL_Global_Forwarding" title="DHL Global Forwarding">DHL Global</a>'s Oceanic distribution warehouse is located in Brisbane, as is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asia_Pacific" title="Asia Pacific">Asia Pacific</a> Aerospace's headquarters. Home grown major companies include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suncorp-Metway_Limited" title="Suncorp-Metway Limited">Suncorp-Metway Limited</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flight_Centre" title="Flight Centre">Flight Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunsuper" title="Sunsuper">Sunsuper</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orrcon" title="Orrcon">Orrcon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Credit_Union_Australia" title="Credit Union Australia">Credit Union Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Australia" title="Boeing Australia">Boeing Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donut_King" title="Donut King">Donut King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wotif.com" title="Wotif.com">Wotif.com</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WebCentral" title="WebCentral">WebCentral</a>, <a href="/wiki/PIPE_Networks" title="PIPE Networks">PIPE Networks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krome_Studios" title="Krome Studios">Krome Studios</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mincom_Limited" title="Mincom Limited">Mincom Limited</a>, <a href="/wiki/TechnologyOne" title="TechnologyOne">TechnologyOne</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thiess_Pty_Ltd" title="Thiess Pty Ltd">Thiess Pty Ltd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a>. Brisbane has the fourth highest <a href="/wiki/Median_household_income_in_Australia_and_New_Zealand" title="Median household income in Australia and New Zealand">median household income</a> of the Australian capital cities at AUD 57,772.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port_of_Brisbane">Port of Brisbane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Port of Brisbane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Brisbane" title="Port of Brisbane">Port of Brisbane</a> is on the lower reaches of the Brisbane River and on Fisherman's Island at the rivers mouth, and is the 3rd most important port in Australia for value of goods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Containerization" title="Containerization">Container freight</a>, sugar, grain, coal and bulk liquids are the major exports. Most of the port facilities are less than three decades old and some are built on reclaimed <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangroves</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wetlands" title="Wetlands">wetlands</a>.</p>
<p>The Port is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Australia_TradeCoast" title="Australia TradeCoast">Australia TradeCoast</a>, the country's fastest-growing economic development area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TradeCoast_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-TradeCoast-81">[81]</a></sup> Geographically, Australia TradeCoast occupies a large swathe of land around the airport and port. Commercially, the area has attracted a mix of companies from throughout the Asia Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TradeCoast_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-TradeCoast-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Brisbane" title="Demographics of Brisbane">Demographics of Brisbane</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_Mall,_Brisbane.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3118" data-file-width="2338" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinatown_Mall%2C_Brisbane.jpg/150px-Chinatown_Mall%2C_Brisbane.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinatown_Mall%2C_Brisbane.jpg/225px-Chinatown_Mall%2C_Brisbane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Chinatown_Mall%2C_Brisbane.jpg/300px-Chinatown_Mall%2C_Brisbane.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_Mall,_Brisbane.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Brisbane" title="Chinatown, Brisbane">Chinatown, Brisbane</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane's Greater Capital City Statistical Area includes the Local Government Areas of <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brisbane" title="City of Brisbane">City of Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Ipswich" title="City of Ipswich">City of Ipswich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moreton_Bay_Region" title="Moreton Bay Region">Moreton Bay Region</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logan_City" title="Logan City">Logan City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Redland_City" title="Redland City">Redland City</a>, as well as parts of <a href="/wiki/Lockyer_Valley_Region" title="Lockyer Valley Region">Lockyer Valley Region</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scenic_Rim_Region" title="Scenic Rim Region">Scenic Rim Region</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Region" title="Somerset Region">Somerset Region</a>, which form a continuous metropolitan area. The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Bureau_of_Statistics" title="Australian Bureau of Statistics">Australian Bureau of Statistics</a> estimates that the population of Greater Brisbane is 2,274,600 as of June 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The 2011 census reported 2,065,996 residents within the Brisbane GCCSA, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Australia_by_population" title="List of cities in Australia by population">third largest city</a> in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Brisbane recorded the second highest growth rate of all capital cities since the previous Census, growing by 11.5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2011 census showed that 2% of Brisbane's population were of indigenous origin and 29.7% were <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Australia" title="Immigration to Australia">born overseas</a>. Of those born outside of Australia, the four most prevalent countries of birth were the United Kingdom, New Zealand, India, and Mainland China. About 17.9% of households spoke a language other than English, with the most common languages being Mandarin 1.5%, Vietnamese 0.9%, Cantonese 0.9%, Samoan 0.6% and Spanish 0.6%.</p>
