<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Areas with significant overseas-born populations predominate in the southern suburbs and inner Brisbane. By far the largest ethnic minority are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Australian" title="Asian Australian">Asian Australians</a>. The area around <a href="/wiki/Sunnybank,_Queensland" title="Sunnybank, Queensland">Sunnybank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunnybank_Hills,_Queensland" title="Sunnybank Hills, Queensland">Sunnybank Hills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stretton,_Queensland" title="Stretton, Queensland">Stretton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robertson,_Queensland" title="Robertson, Queensland">Robertson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calamvale,_Queensland" title="Calamvale, Queensland">Calamvale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macgregor,_Queensland" title="Macgregor, Queensland">Macgregor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eight_Mile_Plains,_Queensland" title="Eight Mile Plains, Queensland">Eight Mile Plains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Runcorn,_Queensland" title="Runcorn, Queensland">Runcorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rochedale,_Queensland" title="Rochedale, Queensland">Rochedale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Mount_Gravatt,_Queensland" title="Upper Mount Gravatt, Queensland">Upper Mount Gravatt</a> is home to a large proportion of Brisbane's Taiwan, Hong Kong, and Mainland China-born population. Brisbane's ethnic Chinese population has traditionally been dominated by those with origins in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and Hong Kong. Ethnic Chinese with origins in Mainland China, Malaysia and other Southeast Asian countries are more spread around the metropolitan area, with the area around <a href="/wiki/St_Lucia,_Queensland" title="St Lucia, Queensland">St Lucia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toowong,_Queensland" title="Toowong, Queensland">Toowong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indooroopilly,_Queensland" title="Indooroopilly, Queensland">Indooroopilly</a> forming a major ethnic Chinese hub in the inner-west, along with the area around <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ommaney,_Queensland" title="Mount Ommaney, Queensland">Mount Ommaney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Park,_Queensland" title="Middle Park, Queensland">Middle Park</a> in the south-west.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Brisbane has the highest population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Australian" title="Taiwanese Australian">Taiwanese Australian</a> citizens of any city in Australia, and the highest proportion of Korean Australians outside of Sydney. A significant portion of Brisbane's Vietnamese population reside in the area around <a href="/wiki/Darra,_Queensland" title="Darra, Queensland">Darra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inala,_Queensland" title="Inala, Queensland">Inala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durack,_Queensland" title="Durack, Queensland">Durack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxley,_Queensland" title="Oxley, Queensland">Oxley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richlands,_Queensland" title="Richlands, Queensland">Richlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forest_Lake,_Queensland" title="Forest Lake, Queensland">Forest Lake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamboree_Heights,_Queensland" title="Jamboree Heights, Queensland">Jamboree Heights</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorooka" title="Moorooka">Moorooka</a> is home to many residents of African descent, while the area around <a href="/wiki/Logan_Central,_Queensland" title="Logan Central, Queensland">Logan Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodridge,_Queensland" title="Woodridge, Queensland">Woodridge</a> is home to a large number of Aboriginal, Maori and Pacific Islanders of which Brisbane has the highest proportion of any Australian capital city. The inner southern suburbs are traditionally considered the most densely populated with people of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_European" title="Southern European">Southern European</a> heritage. There are also a large number of <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filipinos" title="Filipinos">Filipinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Australians" title="German Australians">German Australians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fijians" title="Fijians">Fijians</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific Islander</a> communities in the city.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Queensland" title="List of schools in Queensland">List of schools in Queensland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Queensland,_Brisbane,_Australia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/University_of_Queensland%2C_Brisbane%2C_Australia.jpg/220px-University_of_Queensland%2C_Brisbane%2C_Australia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/University_of_Queensland%2C_Brisbane%2C_Australia.jpg/330px-University_of_Queensland%2C_Brisbane%2C_Australia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/University_of_Queensland%2C_Brisbane%2C_Australia.jpg/440px-University_of_Queensland%2C_Brisbane%2C_Australia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Queensland,_Brisbane,_Australia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Queensland" title="University of Queensland">University of Queensland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane has multi-campus universities and colleges including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Queensland" title="University of Queensland">University of Queensland</a> (UQ), <a href="/wiki/Queensland_University_of_Technology" title="Queensland University of Technology">Queensland University of Technology</a> (QUT) and <a href="/wiki/Griffith_University" title="Griffith University">Griffith University</a>, all among Australia's highest rated universities. Other universities which have campuses in Brisbane include the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Catholic_University" title="Australian Catholic University">Australian Catholic University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Queensland_University" title="Central Queensland University">Central Queensland University</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_University" title="James Cook University">James Cook University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_Queensland" title="University of Southern Queensland">University of Southern Queensland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Sunshine_Coast" title="University of the Sunshine Coast">University of the Sunshine Coast</a>. Brisbane is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Centre_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Aboriginal Centre for the Performing Arts">Aboriginal Centre for the Performing Arts</a>.</p>
<p>There are three major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TAFE" title="TAFE">TAFE</a> colleges in Brisbane; the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_North_Institute_of_TAFE" title="Brisbane North Institute of TAFE">Brisbane North Institute of TAFE</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_South_Institute_of_TAFE" title="Metropolitan South Institute of TAFE">Metropolitan South Institute of TAFE</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Southbank_Institute" title="Southbank Institute">Southbank Institute of TAFE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Brisbane is also home to numerous other independent tertiary providers, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_College_of_Natural_Medicine" title="Australian College of Natural Medicine">Australian College of Natural Medicine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_College_of_Theology" title="Brisbane College of Theology">Brisbane College of Theology</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=QANTM&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="QANTM (page does not exist)">QANTM</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jazz_Music_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jazz Music Institute (page does not exist)">Jazz Music Institute</a>, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jschool:_Journalism_Education_%26_Training" title="Jschool: Journalism Education &amp; Training">Jschool: Journalism Education &amp; Training</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=JMC_Academy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="JMC Academy (page does not exist)">JMC Academy</a>.</p>
<p>Many of Brisbane's <a href="/wiki/Preschool" title="Preschool">preschool</a>, primary, and secondary schools are under the jurisdiction of Education Queensland, a branch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queensland_Government" title="Queensland Government">Queensland Government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> There are also a large number of independent (private), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, Lutheran, and other Christian run schools.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Brisbane" title="Transport in Brisbane">Transport in Brisbane</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG/220px-HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG/330px-HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG/440px-HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HoughtonHighwayEveningPeak.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Houghton_Highway" title="Houghton Highway">Houghton Highway</a>, the second longest bridge in Australia, during peak hour</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane has an extensive transportation network within the city, as well as connections to regional centres, interstate and to overseas destinations. The use of urban public transport is still only a small component of total passenger transport, the largest component being travel by private car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Public transport is provided by bus, rail and ferry services. Bus services are operated by public and private operators whereas trains and ferries are operated by public agencies. The <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_central_business_district" title="Brisbane central business district">Brisbane central business district</a> (CBD) is the central hub for all public transport services with services focusing on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Street_bus_station,_Brisbane" title="Queen Street bus station, Brisbane">Queen Street Bus Station</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roma_Street_railway_station,_Brisbane" title="Roma Street railway station, Brisbane">Roma Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_railway_station,_Brisbane" title="Central railway station, Brisbane">Central</a> railway stations, and various city ferries wharves. Brisbane's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CityCat" title="CityCat">CityCat</a> high speed ferry service, popular with tourists and commuters, operates services along the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River" title="Brisbane River">Brisbane River</a> between the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Queensland" title="University of Queensland">University of Queensland</a> and Apollo Road.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Rail_City_network" title="Queensland Rail City network">Queensland Rail City network</a> network consists of 10 suburban lines and covers mostly the west, north and east sides of the city. It also provides the route for an <a href="/wiki/Airport_railway_line,_Brisbane" title="Airport railway line, Brisbane">Airtrain</a> service under joint public/private control between the City and <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Airport" title="Brisbane Airport">Brisbane Airport</a>. Since 2000, Brisbane has been developing a <a href="/wiki/Busways_in_Brisbane" title="Busways in Brisbane">busway network</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Busway" title="South East Busway">South East Busway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Busway,_Brisbane" title="Northern Busway, Brisbane">Northern Busway</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Busway,_Brisbane" title="Eastern Busway, Brisbane">Eastern Busway</a>. <a href="/wiki/TransLink_(South_East_Queensland)" title="TransLink (South East Queensland)">TransLink</a> operates an <a href="/wiki/Integrated_ticketing" title="Integrated ticketing">integrated ticketing</a> system across the public transport network.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1820" data-file-width="3455" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg/220px-Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg/330px-Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg/440px-Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spirit_of_Brisbane_ferry.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Transdev_Brisbane_Ferries" title="Transdev Brisbane Ferries">Spirit of Brisbane</a> ferry on the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River" title="Brisbane River">Brisbane River</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Brisbane River has created a barrier to some road transport routes. In total there are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridges_of_Brisbane" title="Bridges of Brisbane">ten road bridges</a>, mostly concentrated in the inner city area. This has intensified the need for transport routes to focus on the inner city. There are also three railway bridges and two pedestrian bridges. The <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Schonell_Bridge" title="Eleanor Schonell Bridge">Eleanor Schonell Bridge</a> (originally named, and still generally known as, The Green Bridge) between the University of Queensland and <a href="/wiki/Dutton_Park,_Queensland" title="Dutton Park, Queensland">Dutton Park</a> is for use by buses, pedestrians and cyclists. There are currently multiple tunnel and bridge projects underway as part of the <a href="/wiki/TransApex" title="TransApex">TransApex</a> plan.</p>
<p>An extensive network of pedestrian and cyclist pathways have been created along the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River" title="Brisbane River">Brisbane River</a> to form a <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_River#Brisbane_Riverwalk" title="Brisbane River">Riverwalk</a> network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG/220px-QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG/330px-QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG/440px-QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:QRPassenger_Suburban_Multiple_Unit_265.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Suburban_Multiple_Unit_(Queensland_Rail)" title="Suburban Multiple Unit (Queensland Rail)">Queensland Rail Suburban Multiple Unit</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nambour_railway_station,_Queensland" title="Nambour railway station, Queensland">Nambour Station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane is served by several urban and inter-urban motorways. The <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Motorway_(Brisbane%E2%80%93Brunswick_Heads)" title="Pacific Motorway (Brisbane–Brunswick Heads)">Pacific Motorway</a> connects the central city with the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a> to the south. The <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Motorway" title="Ipswich Motorway">Ipswich Motorway</a> connects the city with Ipswich to the west via the southern suburbs, while the <a href="/wiki/Western_Freeway,_Brisbane" title="Western Freeway, Brisbane">Western Freeway</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centenary_Motorway,_Brisbane" title="Centenary Motorway, Brisbane">Centenary Motorway</a> provide a connection between Brisbane's inner-west and the outer south-west, connecting with the Ipswich Motorway south of the Brisbane River. The <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Highway" title="Bruce Highway">Bruce Highway</a> is Brisbane's main route north of the city to the rest of the State. The Bruce Highway terminates 1,700 km (1,056 mi) away in <a href="/wiki/Cairns" title="Cairns">Cairns</a> and passes through most major cities along the Queensland coast. The <a href="/wiki/Gateway_Motorway" title="Gateway Motorway">Gateway Motorway</a> is a private <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll road</a> which connects the Gold Coast and <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Coast,_Queensland" title="Sunshine Coast, Queensland">Sunshine Coasts</a> by providing an alternate route via the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gateway_Bridge" title="Gateway Bridge">Gateway Bridge</a> avoiding Brisbane's inner city area. The Port of Brisbane Motorway links the Gateway to the Port of Brisbane, while Inner City Bypass and the Riverside Expressway act as the inner ring freeway system to prevent motorists from travelling through the city's congested centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brisbane's population growth placed strains on South East Queensland's transport system. The State Government and Brisbane City Council have responded with infrastructure plans and increased funding for transportation projects, such as the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Queensland_Infrastructure_Plan_and_Program" title="South East Queensland Infrastructure Plan and Program">South East Queensland Infrastructure Plan and Program</a>. Most of the focus has been placed on expanding current road infrastructure, particularly tunnels and bypasses, as well as improving the public transport system.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Airport" title="Brisbane Airport">Brisbane Airport</a> (IATA code: <i>BNE</i>) is the city's main airport, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Australia" title="List of the busiest airports in Australia">third busiest in Australia</a> after <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Airport" title="Sydney Airport">Sydney Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Airport" title="Melbourne Airport">Melbourne Airport</a>. It is located north-east of the city centre and provides domestic and international passenger services. In the 2012–2012 year, Brisbane Airport handled over 21.3 million passengers. The airport is served by <a href="/wiki/Airport_railway_line,_Brisbane" title="Airport railway line, Brisbane">the Brisbane Airtrain</a>, which provides a rail service from Brisbane's city centre to and from the airport. <a href="/wiki/Archerfield_Airport" title="Archerfield Airport">Archerfield Airport</a> (in Brisbane's southern suburbs) acts as a <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> airport.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="2176" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg/600px-King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg/900px-King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg/1200px-King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg 2x" width="600"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:King_George_Square_Busway_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
King George Square Busway Station, an underground bus station</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities_and_healthcare">Utilities and healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Utilities and healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2500" data-file-width="4756" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg/220px-Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg/330px-Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg/440px-Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wivenhoe_Dam_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lake_Wivenhoe" title="Lake Wivenhoe">Lake Wivenhoe</a>, Brisbane's primary water reserve</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Water storage, treatment and delivery for Brisbane is handled by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SEQ_Water" title="SEQ Water">SEQ Water</a>, which sells on to <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Urban_Utilities" title="Queensland Urban Utilities">Queensland Urban Utilities</a> (previously Brisbane Water) for distribution to the greater Brisbane area. Water for the area is stored in one of three dams; <a href="/wiki/Wivenhoe_Dam" title="Wivenhoe Dam">Wivenhoe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Somerset" title="Lake Somerset">Somerset</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Pine_Dam" title="North Pine Dam">North Pine</a>. Since 13 May 2005, Brisbane has enforced <a href="/wiki/Water_restrictions_in_Australia" title="Water restrictions in Australia">water restrictions</a> due to drought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> This has also led to the State Government announcing that purified recycled water would be pumped into the dams once the pipeline was complete in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> More recently, restrictions were lifted and water conservation is no longer a major concern of council, although residents are asked to follow permanent conservation measures.</p>
<p>Electricity and gas grids in Brisbane are handled by <a href="/wiki/Energex" title="Energex">Energex</a> (electricity), and <a href="/wiki/Origin_Energy" title="Origin Energy">Origin Energy</a> (gas), with each company previously holding a monopoly on domestic retail supply. Since 1 July 2007 Queensland regulation changes have opened up the retail energy market, allowing multiple companies to resell both gas and electricity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="708" data-file-width="1156" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg/220px-Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg/330px-Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg/440px-Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mmh-%26-mch-complex.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial of part of Mater Health Services campus at South Brisbane</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Metropolitan Brisbane is serviced by all major and most minor telecommunications companies and their networks. Brisbane has the largest number of enabled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DSL" title="DSL">DSL</a> telephone exchanges in Queensland. An increasing number are also enabled with special hardware (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DSLAM" title="DSLAM">DSLAMs</a>) which enable high speed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ADSL2%2B" title="ADSL2+">ADSL2+</a> internet access. The Brisbane CBD also features a complete underground <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fibre_optics" title="Fibre optics">fibre optics</a> network, with numerous connections to the inner suburbs provided by various service providers.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Telstra" title="Telstra">Telstra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Optus" title="Optus">Optus</a> provide both high speed internet as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pay_TV" title="Pay TV">Pay TV</a> through their cable services for the bulk of the city's metropolitan area. Both of these providers also host wireless networks with <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(Wi-Fi)" title="Hotspot (Wi-Fi)">hotspots</a> within both the inner and suburban areas. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Telstra" title="Telstra">Telstra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optus" title="Optus">Optus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vodafone" title="Vodafone">Vodafone</a> all operate both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2.5G" title="2.5G">2.5G</a>, <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3.5G" title="3.5G">3.5G</a> mobile phone networks citywide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brisbane is covered by <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Health" title="Queensland Health">Queensland Health</a>'s "Northside" and "Southside" health service areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Within the greater Brisbane area there are 8 major <a href="/wiki/Public_hospital" title="Public hospital">public hospitals</a>, 4 major <a href="/wiki/Private_hospital" title="Private hospital">private hospitals</a>, and smaller public and private facilities. Specialist and <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">general</a> medical practices are located in the CBD, and most suburbs and localities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aged_care">Aged care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Aged care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2015 <a href="/wiki/Graham_Quirk" title="Graham Quirk">Lord Mayor Graham Quirk</a> announced plans to offer incentives for developers to build aged care and retirement facilities in some of the city's inner-suburban neighbourhoods. The scheme was based on the discounts for student accommodation infrastructure charges Quirk claimed had energised the student accommodation sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In late August 2016 Quirk announced incentives reducing development infrastructure charges by 33 per cent for a three-year period and allowance for additional two storeys in medium and high density locations "where best practice design standards are met". The reason given was to enable people in inner suburban neighbourhoods to retire and go into aged care in the areas where they lived, and to increase aged care rooms and retirement units overall to meet growing demand. The <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brisbane" title="City of Brisbane">Brisbane City Council</a>'s announcement said the 70 plus population of Brisbane was projected to increase by 50 per cent to 2027. The changes require revisions to the City Plan to include a new code for assessing aged care and retirement living development applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brisbane City Council's Labor opposition said the changes would benefit developers rather than consumers, claiming the discounts don't necessarily tend to translate into more affordable property and called for some of the reductions be used to help reduce property purchase prices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The Property Council of Australia said the policy would position Brisbane as a national leader in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aged_care" title="Aged care">aged-care</a> provision and avert a "seniors' housing shortfall".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Major commercial property firm <a href="/wiki/Savills" title="Savills">Savills</a> Brisbane said the critical suburbs to benefit were in Brisbane's "inner middle ring" including <a href="/wiki/Ashgrove,_Queensland" title="Ashgrove, Queensland">Ashgrove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilston,_Queensland" title="Wilston, Queensland">Wilston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wooloowin,_Queensland" title="Wooloowin, Queensland">Wooloowin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coorparoo,_Queensland" title="Coorparoo, Queensland">Coorparoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yeronga,_Queensland" title="Yeronga, Queensland">Yeronga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auchenflower,_Queensland" title="Auchenflower, Queensland">Auchenflower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Casino,_Queensland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Brisbane_Casino%2C_Queensland.jpg/220px-Brisbane_Casino%2C_Queensland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Brisbane_Casino%2C_Queensland.jpg/330px-Brisbane_Casino%2C_Queensland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Brisbane_Casino%2C_Queensland.jpg/440px-Brisbane_Casino%2C_Queensland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treasury_Hotel_and_Casino" title="Treasury Hotel and Casino">Treasury Hotel and Casino</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane has a substantial live theatre and music scene – both popular and classical.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queensland_Gallery_of_Modern_Art">Queensland Gallery of Modern Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Queensland Gallery of Modern Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1718" data-file-width="2576" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG/220px-Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG/330px-Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG/440px-Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gallery_of_Modern_Art_Main_Entrance.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
GOMA, main entrance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Gallery_of_Modern_Art" title="Queensland Gallery of Modern Art">Queensland Gallery of Modern Art</a> (GOMA), opened in December 2006, is one of the latest additions to the <a href="/wiki/South_Bank,_Queensland" title="South Bank, Queensland">South Bank</a> precinct and houses some of the most well-known pieces of modern art from within and outside Australia. GOMA is the largest modern art gallery in Australia. GOMA holds the Asia Pacific Triennial (APT) which focuses on contemporary art from the Asia and Pacific in a variety of media from painting to video work. In Addition, its size enables the gallery to exhibit particularly large shows — the <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">Andy Warhol</a> exhibition being the largest survey of his work in Australia. GOMA also boasts Australia's largest purpose-built Cinémathèque. The Gallery of Modern Art is located next to the <a href="/wiki/State_Library_of_Queensland" title="State Library of Queensland">State Library of Queensland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Art_Gallery" title="Queensland Art Gallery">Queensland Art Gallery</a>. Along with Beijing, Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, Brisbane was nominated as one of the Top 5 International Music Hotspots by <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> in 2007. There are also popular entertainment pubs and clubs within both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane_CBD" title="Brisbane CBD">City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fortitude_Valley,_Queensland" title="Fortitude Valley, Queensland">Fortitude Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_classical_culture">Arts and classical culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Arts and classical culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Arts_and_culture_in_Brisbane" title="Arts and culture in Brisbane">Arts and culture in Brisbane</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:QPAC_Exterior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/QPAC_Exterior.jpg/220px-QPAC_Exterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/QPAC_Exterior.jpg/330px-QPAC_Exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/QPAC_Exterior.jpg/440px-QPAC_Exterior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:QPAC_Exterior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the western face of the Queensland Performing Arts Centre</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues_and_classical_performers">Venues and classical performers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Venues and classical performers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Performing_Arts_Centre" title="Queensland Performing Arts Centre">Queensland Performing Arts Centre</a> (QPAC), which is located at <a href="/wiki/South_Bank,_Queensland" title="South Bank, Queensland">South Bank</a>, consists of the Lyric Theatre, a Concert Hall, Cremorne Theatre and the Playhouse Theatre and is home to the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Ballet" title="Queensland Ballet">Queensland Ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera_Queensland" title="Opera Queensland">Opera Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Theatre_Company" title="Queensland Theatre Company">Queensland Theatre Company</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Queensland Symphony Orchestra">Queensland Symphony Orchestra</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Conservatorium_Griffith_University" title="Queensland Conservatorium Griffith University">Queensland Conservatorium</a>, in which professional companies and Conservatorium students also stage performances, is located within the <a href="/wiki/South_Bank_Parklands" title="South Bank Parklands">South Bank Parklands</a>. Numerous choirs present performances across the city annually. These choirs include the Brisbane Chorale, Queensland Choir, Brisbane Chamber Choir, Canticum Chamber Choir, Brisbane Concert Choir, Imogen Children's Chorale and <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Birralee_Voices" title="Brisbane Birralee Voices">Brisbane Birralee Voices</a>. Due to the lack of a suitable purpose built performance venue for choral music, these choirs typically perform in the city's many churches.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to dramatic and musical theatre performances at QPAC, the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Powerhouse" title="Brisbane Powerhouse">Brisbane Powerhouse</a> in New Farm and the <a href="/wiki/Judith_Wright_Centre_of_Contemporary_Arts" title="Judith Wright Centre of Contemporary Arts">Judith Wright Centre of Contemporary Arts</a> on <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Street,_Brisbane" title="Brunswick Street, Brisbane">Brunswick Street</a> in Fortitude Valley feature diverse programs featuring exhibitions and festivals of visual art, music and dance.</p>
<p>Brisbane is also home to numerous small theatres that provide access to emerging amateur and pro-am artists and companies. The oldest is the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Arts_Theatre" title="Brisbane Arts Theatre">Brisbane Arts Theatre</a> which was founded in 1936. It has a regular adult and children's theatre and is located in <a href="/wiki/Petrie_Terrace,_Queensland" title="Petrie Terrace, Queensland">Petrie Terrace</a>. The <a href="/wiki/La_Boite_Theatre_Company" title="La Boite Theatre Company">La Boite Theatre Company</a> now performs at the <a href="/wiki/Roundhouse_Theatre" title="Roundhouse Theatre">Roundhouse Theatre</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kelvin_Grove,_Queensland" title="Kelvin Grove, Queensland">Kelvin Grove</a>. Other professional theatres in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Twelfth_Night_Theatre" title="Twelfth Night Theatre">Twelfth Night Theatre</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bowen_Hills,_Queensland" title="Bowen Hills, Queensland">Bowen Hills</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Metro_Arts_Theatre" title="Metro Arts Theatre">Metro Arts Theatre</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Edward_Street,_Brisbane" title="Edward Street, Brisbane">Edward Street</a>, and the Queensland Theatre Company's <a href="/wiki/Bille_Brown" title="Bille Brown">Bille Brown</a> Studio in <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Queensland" title="West End, Queensland">West End</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Popular_entertainment_in_Brisbane" title="Popular entertainment in Brisbane">Popular entertainment in Brisbane</a></div>
<p>Brisbane has a substantial live popular music scene.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_music">Live music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Live music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brisbane has maintained a constantly evolving live music scene, producing acts spanning genres including <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_punk_rock" title="Brisbane punk rock">Brisbane punk rock</a>), <a href="/wiki/Indie_rock" title="Indie rock">indie rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noise_rock" title="Noise rock">noise rock</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metal_music" title="Metal music">metal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Post-punk" title="Post-punk">post-punk</a>. Brisbane's live music history is often intertwined with social unrest and authoritarian politics, as retold by journalist Andrew Stafford in <a href="/wiki/Pig_City_(music_festival)#Pig_City_.28book.29" title="Pig City (music festival)"><i>Pig City: From The Saints to Savage Garden</i></a> and in <i>Radical Brisbane: An Unruly History</i>, edited by academics Raymond Evans and <a href="/wiki/Carole_Ferrier" title="Carole Ferrier">Carole Ferrier</a>.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_punk_rock" title="Brisbane punk rock">Brisbane punk rock</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicians">Musicians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Musicians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">Bee Gees</a> were born in the United Kingdom, but raised in <a href="/wiki/Redcliffe,_Queensland" title="Redcliffe, Queensland">Redcliffe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cribb_Island,_Queensland" title="Cribb Island, Queensland">Cribb Island</a>, Brisbane.</li>
<li>The members of <a href="/wiki/Powderfinger" title="Powderfinger">Powderfinger</a> met at <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Grammar_School" title="Brisbane Grammar School">Brisbane Grammar School</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Queensland" title="University of Queensland">University of Queensland</a>, and found early popularity within Brisbane.</li>
<li>Indie band <a href="/wiki/The_Go-Betweens" title="The Go-Betweens">The Go-Betweens</a> (after whom Brisbane's <a href="/wiki/Go_Between_Bridge" title="Go Between Bridge">Go Between Bridge</a> is named) were based out of Brisbane, and many of their songs and albums, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Spring_Hill_Fair" title="Spring Hill Fair">Spring Hill Fair</a></i>, reflect the attitude of 1980s Brisbane.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Veronicas" title="The Veronicas">The Veronicas</a>' <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Origliasso" title="Lisa Origliasso">Lisa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Origliasso" title="Jessica Origliasso">Jessica Origliasso</a> were born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Albany_Creek,_Queensland" title="Albany Creek, Queensland">Albany Creek</a>, Brisbane.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Saints_(Australian_band)" title="The Saints (Australian band)">The Saints</a>, based in Brisbane since 1974, were one of the first <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> bands to form outside the United States.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheppard_(band)" title="Sheppard (band)">Sheppard</a> reached No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Singles Chart</a> after forming in Brisbane in 2009.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Savage_Garden" title="Savage Garden">Savage Garden</a> formed in the 1990s after <a href="/wiki/Darren_Hayes" title="Darren Hayes">Darren Hayes</a> responded to <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Jones_(musician)" title="Daniel Jones (musician)">Daniel Jones</a>' advertisement in a Brisbane newspaper.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_references">Music references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brisbane is featured in music including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Saints_(band)" title="The Saints (band)">The Saints</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Sounds" title="Prehistoric Sounds">Brisbane (Security City)</a>" (1978); <a href="/wiki/The_Stranglers" title="The Stranglers">The Stranglers</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Device_(The_Wizard_of_Aus)" title="Nuclear Device (The Wizard of Aus)">Nuclear Device</a>" (1979) about <a href="/wiki/Joh_Bjelke-Petersen" title="Joh Bjelke-Petersen">Joh Bjelke-Petersen</a>; "Love You Brisbane" theme single from the 1980s;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Midnight_Oil" title="Midnight Oil">Midnight Oil</a>'s single "<a href="/wiki/Dreamworld_(Midnight_Oil_song)" title="Dreamworld (Midnight Oil song)">Dreamworld</a>" (1987); <a href="/wiki/Powderfinger" title="Powderfinger">Powderfinger</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Vulture_Street_(album)" title="Vulture Street (album)">Vulture Street</a></i> (2003).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Brisbane" title="List of people from Brisbane">List of people from Brisbane</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Brisbane" title="Sport in Brisbane">Sport in Brisbane</a></div>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2371" data-file-width="3279" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg/220px-Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg/330px-Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg/440px-Australia_vs_South_Africa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane has hosted several major sporting events including the <a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982 Commonwealth Games</a> and the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Games" title="Goodwill Games">Goodwill Games</a>. The city also hosted events during the <a href="/wiki/1987_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1987 Rugby World Cup">1987 Rugby World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/1992_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1992 Cricket World Cup">1992 Cricket World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Sydney Olympics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a> and hosted the Final of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 Rugby League World Cup</a> and will host along with the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>, some events for the <a href="/wiki/2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="2018 Commonwealth Games">2018 Commonwealth Games</a>. In 2005, then <a href="/wiki/Premier" title="Premier">Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Beattie" title="Peter Beattie">Peter Beattie</a> announced plans for Brisbane to bid to host the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2024_Olympic_Games" title="2024 Olympic Games">2024 Olympic Games</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> which in August 2008 received in principle <a href="/wiki/Australian_Olympic_Committee" title="Australian Olympic Committee">Australian Olympic Committee</a> support, including that of the former Queensland Premier <a href="/wiki/Anna_Bligh" title="Anna Bligh">Anna Bligh</a> and former Brisbane Lord Mayor <a href="/wiki/Campbell_Newman" title="Campbell Newman">Campbell Newman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The most popular professional club in the city is the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Broncos" title="Brisbane Broncos">Brisbane Broncos</a>, who play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> competition. Rugby Union is also very popular in Brisbane and the city hosts the Queensland Reds who play Super Rugby. Brisbane also hosts a professional soccer team named <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar_FC" title="Brisbane Roar FC">Brisbane Roar FC</a> and an AFL club the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a>. Brisbane recently re-introduced their Basketball team the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Bullets" title="Brisbane Bullets">Brisbane Bullets</a> into the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(Australia)" title="National Basketball League (Australia)">National Basketball League (Australia)</a> after a 8 hiatus.</p>
<p>The city's major sporting venues include <a href="/wiki/The_Gabba" title="The Gabba">The Gabba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sleeman_Centre_(Brisbane)" title="Sleeman Centre (Brisbane)">Sleeman Centre</a> at <a href="/wiki/Chandler,_Queensland" title="Chandler, Queensland">Chandler</a>, Suncorp Stadium (<a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Lang Park</a>), <a href="/wiki/Ballymore_Stadium" title="Ballymore Stadium">Ballymore Stadium</a> and the stadium facilities of the <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Sport_and_Athletics_Centre" title="Queensland Sport and Athletics Centre">Queensland Sport and Athletics Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nathan,_Queensland" title="Nathan, Queensland">Nathan</a>. With the closure of the Milton Tennis grounds in 1994, Brisbane lacked a major tennis facility. In 2005, the State Government approved the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tennyson_Tennis_Centre" title="Tennyson Tennis Centre">State Tennis Centre</a> a new A$65 million tennis stadium. The construction was completed in 2008. The <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_International" title="Brisbane International">Brisbane International</a> is held here from January 2009.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Annual_events">Annual events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Annual events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg/220px-Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg/330px-Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg/440px-Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Riverfire_2009_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Festival" title="Brisbane Festival">Riverfire</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Story_Bridge" title="Story Bridge">Story Bridge</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Major cultural events in Brisbane include the <a href="/wiki/Ekka" title="Ekka">Ekka</a> (the Royal Queensland Exhibition), held each August, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverfestival" title="Riverfestival">Riverfestival</a>, held each September at <a href="/wiki/South_Bank_Parklands" title="South Bank Parklands">South Bank Parklands</a> and surrounding areas. Warana (meaning <i>Blue Skies</i>) was a former spring festival which began in 1961 and was held in September each year. Run as a celebration of Brisbane, Warana was similar to Melbourne's <a href="/wiki/Moomba" title="Moomba">Moomba</a> festival. In 1996 the annual festival was changed to a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Biennial" title="wikt:Biennial">biennial</a> Brisbane Festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_International_Film_Festival" title="Brisbane International Film Festival">Brisbane International Film Festival</a> (BIFF) is held in July/August in a variety of venues around Brisbane. BIFF features new films and retrospectives by domestic and international filmmakers along with seminars and awards.</p>
<p>The Paniyiri festival at <a href="/wiki/Musgrave_Park,_Brisbane" title="Musgrave Park, Brisbane">Musgrave Park</a> (corner of Russell and Edmondstone Streets, <a href="/wiki/South_Brisbane,_Queensland" title="South Brisbane, Queensland">South Brisbane</a>) is an annual Greek cultural festival held over two days in May. The Brisbane Medieval Fayre and Tournament is held each June in <a href="/wiki/Musgrave_Park,_Brisbane" title="Musgrave Park, Brisbane">Musgrave Park</a>. The Valley Fiesta is an annual three-day event organised by the Valley Chamber of Commerce. It was launched by Brisbane Marketing in 2002 to promote Fortitude Valley as a hub for arts and youth culture. It features free live music, market stalls, food and drink from many local restaurants and cafés, and other entertainment. The <a href="/wiki/Bridge_to_Brisbane" title="Bridge to Brisbane">Bridge to Brisbane</a> fun run has become a major annual charity event for Brisbane. The <a href="/wiki/Caxton_Street_Seafood_and_Wine_Festival" title="Caxton Street Seafood and Wine Festival">Caxton Street Seafood and Wine Festival</a> was launched in 1994 by the Caxton Street Development Association to promote Caxton Street in historic Petrie Terrace as a significant entertainment precinct that celebrates and promotes Australian music, seafood and wine. It features live music, food and drink from Caxton Street restaurants and cafés, as well as Art Exhibitions and Historical Displays and a dedicated annual Festival Band Competition. The annual <a href="/wiki/Buddha%27s_Birthday" title="Buddha's Birthday">Buddha Birth Day</a> festival at Brisbane's South Bank is thought to be the world's largest, attracting over 200,000 visitors each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The organisers of that festival are not a reliable source. (July 2015)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_and_recreation">Tourism and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tourism and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Brisbane" title="Tourism in Brisbane">Tourism in Brisbane</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1703" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg/220px-Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg/330px-Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg/440px-Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_City_Botanic_Gardens_lawn.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/City_Botanic_Gardens" title="City Botanic Gardens">City Botanic Gardens</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tourism plays a major role in Brisbane's economy, being the third-most popular destination for international tourists after Sydney and Melbourne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Popular tourist and recreation areas in Brisbane include the <a href="/wiki/South_Bank_Parklands" title="South Bank Parklands">South Bank Parklands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roma_Street_Parkland" title="Roma Street Parkland">Roma Street Parkland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/City_Botanic_Gardens" title="City Botanic Gardens">City Botanic Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Forest_Park" title="Brisbane Forest Park">Brisbane Forest Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portside_Wharf" title="Portside Wharf">Portside Wharf</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lone_Pine_Koala_Sanctuary" title="Lone Pine Koala Sanctuary">Lone Pine Koala Sanctuary</a> opened in 1927 and was the world's first koala sanctuary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thenandnow2_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-thenandnow2-116">[116]</a></sup> The suburb of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Coot-tha,_Queensland" title="Mount Coot-tha, Queensland">Mount Coot-tha</a> is home to a popular state forest, and the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Botanic_Gardens,_Mount_Coot-tha" title="Brisbane Botanic Gardens, Mount Coot-tha">Brisbane Botanic Gardens</a> which houses the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Brisbane_Planetarium" title="Sir Thomas Brisbane Planetarium">Sir Thomas Brisbane Planetarium</a> and the "Tsuki-yama-chisen" Japanese Garden (formerly of the Japanese Government Pavilion of Brisbane's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expo_%2788" title="Expo '88">World Expo '88</a>).</p>
<p>Brisbane has over 27 km (17 mi) of bicycle pathways, mostly surrounding the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane_river" title="Brisbane river">Brisbane river</a> and city centre, extending to the west of the city. The river itself was popular with bathers, and it permitted boating excursions to Moreton Bay when the main port was in the city reaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thenandnow2_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-thenandnow2-116">[116]</a></sup> Today fishing and boating are more common. Other popular recreation activities include the <a href="/wiki/Story_Bridge" title="Story Bridge">Story Bridge</a> adventure climb and rock climbing at the <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_Point_Cliffs" title="Kangaroo Point Cliffs">Kangaroo Point Cliffs</a>. The nearby <a href="/wiki/Australia_Zoo" title="Australia Zoo">Australia Zoo</a>, made famous by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Irwin" title="Steve Irwin">Steve Irwin</a>, also encourages many tourists to visit Brisbane.</p>
<p>In 2015, a competition by travel guidebook <i><a href="/wiki/Rough_Guides" title="Rough Guides">Rough Guides</a></i> saw Brisbane elected as one of the top ten most beautiful cities in the world, citing reasons such as "its winning combination of high-rise modern architecture, lush green spaces and the enormous Brisbane River that snakes its way through the centre before emptying itself into the azure Moreton Bay."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Print">Print</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Print">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The main newspapers of Brisbane are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Courier-Mail" title="The Courier-Mail">The Courier-Mail</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Mail_(Brisbane)" title="The Sunday Mail (Brisbane)">The Sunday Mail</a></i>, both owned by <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation" title="News Corporation">News Corporation</a>. Brisbane receives the national daily, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian" title="The Australian">The Australian</a></i>, and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weekend_Australian" title="Weekend Australian">Weekend Australian</a></i>, together with <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_Media" title="Fairfax Media">Fairfax</a> papers <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Financial_Review" title="Australian Financial Review">Australian Financial Review</a></i>, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sydney_Morning_Herald" title="Sydney Morning Herald">Sydney Morning Herald</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Age" title="The Age">The Age</a></i>, and Fairfax website <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Times" title="Brisbane Times">Brisbane Times</a>. There are community and suburban newspapers throughout the metropolitan and regional areas, including <i>Brisbane News</i> and <i>City News</i>, many of which are produced by <a href="/wiki/Quest_Community_Newspapers" title="Quest Community Newspapers">Quest Community Newspapers</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/MX_(newspaper)" title="MX (newspaper)">mX</a></i>, a free daily commuter newspaper, was launched in 2007, following the newspaper's success in Melbourne and Sydney.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Brisbane is served by all five major television networks in Australia, which broadcast from the summit of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Coot-tha,_Queensland" title="Mount Coot-tha, Queensland">Mount Coot-tha</a>. The three commercial stations, <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nine_Network" title="Nine Network">Nine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Network_Ten" title="Network Ten">Ten</a>, are accompanied by two government networks, <a href="/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Australian Broadcasting Corporation">ABC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service" title="Special Broadcasting Service">SBS</a>, with all five providing <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital television</a>. Channels available in addition to ABC, Seven, Nine, Ten and SBS include <a href="/wiki/One_(Australian_TV_channel)" title="One (Australian TV channel)">One</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleven_(TV_channel)" title="Eleven (TV channel)">Eleven</a>, <a href="/wiki/TVSN" title="TVSN">TVSN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spree_TV" title="Spree TV">Spree TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABC2" title="ABC2">ABC2/KIDS</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC3" title="ABC3">ABC3</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABC_News_24" title="ABC News 24">ABC News 24</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SBS_HD" title="SBS HD">SBS HD</a> (SBS broadcast in HD), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SBS2" title="SBS2">SBS2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_Network_(Australia)" title="Food Network (Australia)">Food Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Indigenous_Television" title="National Indigenous Television">NITV</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7Two" title="7Two">7Two</a>, <a href="/wiki/7mate" title="7mate">7mate</a>, <a href="/wiki/7flix" title="7flix">7flix</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TV4ME" title="TV4ME">TV4ME</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racing.com" title="Racing.com">RACING.COM</a>, <a href="/wiki/9HD" title="9HD">9HD</a> (Nine broadcast in HD), <a href="/wiki/9Gem" title="9Gem">9Gem</a>, <a href="/wiki/9Go!" title="9Go!">9Go!</a>, <a href="/wiki/9Life" title="9Life">9Life</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extra_(Australian_TV_channel)" title="Extra (Australian TV channel)">eXtra</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/31_Brisbane" title="31 Brisbane">31</a>, a community station, also broadcasts in Brisbane. <a href="/wiki/Optus" title="Optus">Optus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foxtel" title="Foxtel">Foxtel</a> operate PayTV services in Brisbane, via <a href="/wiki/Cable" title="Cable">cable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> means.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Australian Broadcasting Corporation">ABC</a> transmits all five of its radio networks to Brisbane; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/612_ABC_Brisbane" title="612 ABC Brisbane">612 ABC Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABC_Classic_FM" title="ABC Classic FM">ABC Classic FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABC_NewsRadio" title="ABC NewsRadio">ABC NewsRadio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_National" title="Radio National">Radio National</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Triple_J" title="Triple J">Triple J</a>. <a href="/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service" title="Special Broadcasting Service">SBS</a> broadcasts its national radio network. Brisbane is serviced by major commercial radio stations, including <a href="/wiki/4KQ" title="4KQ">4KQ</a>, 4BC, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4BH" title="4BH">4BH</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/97.3_FM_(ARN)" title="97.3 FM (ARN)">97.3 FM</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B105_FM" title="B105 FM">B105 FM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_106.9" title="Nova 106.9">Nova 106.9</a>, RadioTAB and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple_M" title="Triple M">Triple M</a>. Brisbane is also serviced by major community radio stations such as <a href="/wiki/96five_Family_FM" title="96five Family FM">96five Family FM</a>, 4MBS Classic FM 103.7, 4EB FM and <a href="/wiki/4ZZZ" title="4ZZZ">4ZZZ</a> 102.1. Additional channels are also available via DAB Digital Radio.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brisbane_nicknames">Brisbane nicknames</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Brisbane nicknames">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Bris Vegas" is an ironic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> nickname given to the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brisres_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-brisres-121">[121]</a></sup> This has been attributed to an <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> tribute CD<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vivab_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-vivab-122">[122]</a></sup> and the city's growing live music scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billb_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-billb-123">[123]</a></sup> It is believed to have been first used in print in a 1996 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Courier-Mail" title="The Courier-Mail">The Courier-Mail</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vivab_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-vivab-122">[122]</a></sup> also about the time of the opening of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conrad_Treasury_Casino" title="Conrad Treasury Casino">Treasury Casino</a> in Brisbane and the popularisation of poker machines in Brisbane bars and clubs, a play on the popular gaming ground of <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>. The name has also been attributed to the city's nightlife,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cg_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-cg-124">[124]</a></sup> compact size of the central business district and perceived lack of sophistication, a comparison to the ostensibly <a href="/wiki/Kitsch" title="Kitsch">kitsch</a> and crass Las Vegas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brisres_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-brisres-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aap_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-aap-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-name-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
